    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <span id="freeText9462930067867391497" style="display:none">Most high school sports teams have rivalries with other schools. At Hamilton High, it's a civil war: the football team versus the soccer team. And for her part, Lissa is sick of it. Her quarterback boyfriend, Randy, is always ditching her to go pick a fight with the soccer team or to prank their locker room. And on three separate occasions Randy's car has been egged while he and Lissa were inside, making out. She is done competing with a bunch of sweaty boys for her own boyfriend's attention.<br /><br />Lissa decides to end the rivalry once and for all: She and the other players' girlfriends go on a hookup strike. The boys won't get any action from them until the football and soccer teams make peace. What they don't count on is a new sort of rivalry: an impossible girls-against-boys showdown that hinges on who will cave to their libidos first. And Lissa never sees her own sexual tension with the leader of the boys, Cash Sterling, coming.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_154983761" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154983761" />
    <a title="Lamia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4804393-lamia"><img alt="Lamia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294943987p2/4804393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154983761?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lamia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lamia" href="/user/show/4804393-lamia">Lamia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4804393-lamia?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154983761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12071711319567722176">You know there's something wrong with a book when the boys are falling all over themselves for the main character and you're wondering why.<br/>I guess Lissa was okay at first. For the first half, maybe. But then she turned into this huge caricature who just lost all intelligence and became obsessed with winning the "war" and finding every pretext to feel sorry for herself. I am aware not all teenagers are sensible, responsible beings. I do, however, like to actually feel something other than annoyan</span>
  <span id="freeText12071711319567722176" style="display:none">You know there's something wrong with a book when the boys are falling all over themselves for the main character and you're wondering why.<br />I guess Lissa was okay at first. For the first half, maybe. But then she turned into this huge caricature who just lost all intelligence and became obsessed with winning the "war" and finding every pretext to feel sorry for herself. I am aware not all teenagers are sensible, responsible beings. I do, however, like to actually feel something other than annoyance for a book narrator. Which is sadly all that I felt here.<br /><br />Another qualm I have about this book: it felt like a giant feminist manifesto. <br />Let me explain. I don't know if you've ever read one of Kody's blog articles, but she heavily denounces the disparity between males and females when talking about sex. And I do like her blog posts. I agree with her whole-heartedly, it <i>is</i> unfair. BUT, as a reader, I really don't need to be lectured all the way through the novel. I do understand that literature is one of the ways you can change people's mentality, but in this case, it was so completely blatant that I felt I was reading the author's views more than the character's. Which is a shame, really, as I would have loved reading a book delivering the same content, with, you know. Craft and subtlety.<br /><br />I was actually going to give this one 2 stars, but Lissa managed to heighten my frustration to such spectacular levels at the end that I just couldn't even give it that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12071711319567722176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1200221237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1200221237" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1200221237?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1200221237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4570097029412513273"><b>3.5 stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/96dc4a1a-bfe0-4415-95e9-b1f7f0002604_zpstwlzor3o.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435925814i/15391603.jpg' alt=' photo 96dc4a1a-bfe0-4415-95e9-b1f7f0002604_zpstwlzor3o.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Shut Out</i> is one of those books that was so fun to listen to! This is the second book of Kody Keplinger's I've read (Duff being the first) and I have to say I love her style. She writes fun reads with just enough seriousness/emotion to keep me invested. But they're also on the light side and entertaining. This was just the type of story I was in the mood for!<br/><br/>Lissa is sick of the feud at her school. Soccer boys vs. Football boys. It's been going on too long. It's effecting her and he</span>
  <span id="freeText4570097029412513273" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/96dc4a1a-bfe0-4415-95e9-b1f7f0002604_zpstwlzor3o.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1435925814i/15391603.jpg" alt=" photo 96dc4a1a-bfe0-4415-95e9-b1f7f0002604_zpstwlzor3o.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Shut Out</i> is one of those books that was so fun to listen to! This is the second book of Kody Keplinger's I've read (Duff being the first) and I have to say I love her style. She writes fun reads with just enough seriousness/emotion to keep me invested. But they're also on the light side and entertaining. This was just the type of story I was in the mood for!<br><br>Lissa is sick of the feud at her school. Soccer boys vs. Football boys. It's been going on too long. It's effecting her and her relationship with her football playing boyfriend. After enough is enough she decides to fight back. She gets together with the girls dating other players from both teams and they unite. They make a pack to 'hold out' until this feud is over. The boys will surely stop this if they're getting cut off, right? It seems like a legit plan but things never seem to go according to plan...<br><br>Lissa was a fantastic heroine. I love the way she was with her family, she reminded me a lot of myself in that regard. Her dad and brother were great, and her best friend Casey had me laughing throughout the story. I loved how her relationship with our hero progressed. The narration was good when it came to Lissa, but anytime she was voicing any other character, not so great. Still, overall this is an audiobook I would recommend and I would definitely recommend reading it for all YA lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4570097029412513273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_206198418" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206198418" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206198418?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of &quot;the DUFF&quot; and maybe even &quot;Not that kind of girl&quot;</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=laugh-aloud">laugh-aloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206198418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11602692883703340024"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kody-keplinger/shut-out-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358464i/709667.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I know why some people might not like this book, I understand the problems they might have with the situations, the characters and so on, but i'm as sure as hell that i did like it, probably as much as I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124395588' title='The DUFF review' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>The DUFF</a>.<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b> (<i>originally posted at <a title='Shut Out Review' href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kody-keplinger/shut-out-review.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadingAfterMidnight</a></i>)<br/><br/>You know, this is a strange world we are living in.<br/>I always read some reviews here and there (about some books - not only this one) and I see people saying that [this] or [that] are not some books that they would allow th</span>
  <span id="freeText11602692883703340024" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kody-keplinger/shut-out-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358464i/709667.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I know why some people might not like this book, I understand the problems they might have with the situations, the characters and so on, but i'm as sure as hell that i did like it, probably as much as I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124395588" title="The DUFF review" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The DUFF</a>.<br><br><b>Full review:</b> (<i>originally posted at <a title="Shut Out Review" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kody-keplinger/shut-out-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight</a></i>)<br><br>You know, this is a strange world we are living in.<br>I always read some reviews here and there (about some books - not only this one) and I see people saying that [this] or [that] are not some books that they would allow their children read, because they include some cuss words or some sex mentioning, and THEN I hear some middle school (yes, MIDDLE SCHOOL!) girls talking about how many boys they are sleeping with.<br>Am I the only one thinking that something is not right?<br><br>Some people think that if the kids don't read about some things, they are somehow protected, but in fact, it is not true, because without you knowing, those kids are doing as much and more, and they get to the point of being clueless, like the characters in this book, not knowing what is normal, and what is not.<br>On the other hand, of course being a good parent is a big responsibility, and it seems to be something hard to achieve - not allowing too much but not being too strict either, and I wouldn't know since I am not a parent yet. But anyways this is raising some questions that have to be answered.<br><br><a href="http://ajw9491.deviantart.com/art/Speak-50356975" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358464i/709668.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Now about the book:<br>This is exactly the kind of book I would have wanted to read in high school.. remember when 2 or 3 (or more) friends of yours were talking about their private life and you couldn't not wonder if there was something wrong with you for not making the same decisions? Well I wish my younger self would have been more sure about her decisions and wouldn't have felt like she was missing something when in fact this is such a private subject that you're the only one who could tell what is good and what is wrong for yourself.. no one else can do that.<br><br>I don't know why it is advertised the way it is, but the content of this books is lighter compared to some other books.<br>SHUT OUT is more <b>about discovering yourself, defining what is 'normal' by your own terms, not letting other people's life control what you want to do, respecting yourself and your body and making decisions based on what makes you feel happy, and comfortable, and safe. It's about the pressure from the others and not letting it bother you, change you, define you.</b><br><br>But I'll start from the beginning, to make some things more clear.<br>The book starts in the middle of the war between the soccer team and the football team. We didn't have any kind of teams back in high school (there were some games between the teachers and the students but those don't count at this point), but I could see this happening.. Boys are always boys, and they don't need the best reasons in the world to pick a fight.<br>The first scene (including some car egging) is, as you might think, absolutely ridiculous, and it only reminded me about how silly boys are in high school and it made me roll my eyes. But from there on, form my part at least, there was not too much eyes-rolling and I found the book to be quite entertaining and fun, and between the words there are also some good messages.<br><br>To put it short, the main character (<b>Lissa</b>) is sick of being second on her boyfriend's list of priorities, she is tired of being lied to, and she is even more annoyed to find out that this "war" is getting people really hurt, so she decides to put an end to it. She talks with the girlfriends of all the other players and decides to not give the boys what they want, until they give up the stupid fight. This sounds pretty easy right?<br>Well, it should be, but then the strike is backfiring in their own faces and the boys with their new "leader" make their own moves, and things get a little more complicated and fun to watch (from time to time a bit ridiculous as well, but fun nevertheless). Of course one of the results was the expected one, and Lissa got a ticket in the first row for it, but the fact that there were some realistic facts in it, made this books so great.<br><br><a href="http://justinetin.deviantart.com/art/Girls-VS-Boys-210368701?q=boost%3Apopular%20boys%20vs%20girls&amp;qo=12" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358464i/709669.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I liked their sleepovers and talking sessions, and I like that everyone felt at some point free to speak their mind, and if they made a decision about their own personal life, no one was there to convince them otherwise.<br>I am of course talking about <b>Mary</b> here - she was sweet and kind, and a bit shy. She knew she wasn't ready to take her relationship to the next level and even when she heard the other girls talking about their experience she still didn't change her mind.<br>At the opposite side we find <b>Chloe</b> - she doesn't have a boyfriend, doesn't need one, never sleeps with someone having a girlfriend and really enjoys one-night-stands. But there was more to her than this. Being Lissa's friend we found more about her, and I wish I could have a friend like her. She was what you call 'a good friend', telling you when you were right or wrong, being supportive but also speaking her mind, always there for her friend no matter what - I guess she was my favorite character in the book (..except from Cash maybe)<br>Another character I liked was <b>Ellen</b> - she and Lissa were best friends before having boyfriends from different sides, but they still cared for each other and showed that with their actions. I liked her even more when she opened Lissa's eyes, making her understand that the strike was meant to stop a fight not create another, making her understand that hurting people is what they were suppose to stop - she was a good friend even after all this time.<br>I should mention <b>Lissa's father</b> too, because I really liked him. It was hard for him to watch for his daughter and the only thing he could do was give her some advices (on some subjects at least). He let her make her own decisions, based on her happiness, and he was as supportive as he could.<br><br>Now back to the boys.. I don't want to spoil everything for you so all I'm going to say is that I would have punched <b>Randy</b> (repeatedly) and I would have hugged <b>Cash</b> (repeatedly*1000). I understand why Lissa felt so safe in a relationship that didn't make her always happy, and I think I know why she liked Cash better (and Oh! I love that scene from the 'last summer'..so sweet :D).<br><br><a href="http://readingaftermidnight.s3.amazonaws.com/wp-content/uploads/2011/09/images-3.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380358464i/709670.jpg" alt="" width="262" height="192" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There were some things that made me really confused and I can't say that I could relate with Lissa (and to begin with, I think that she deserved way more than the backseat of some car at some point - just saying), but I kind of understood her and her actions.<br>It made me sad her confession about needing a mother to talk (or even a stepmother) because she didn't know what was right or wrong and she needed someone to be there for her and give her some advices. I wanted her to have more confidence under that "Ice Queen" appearance, but she was just a kid, it is normal for her to have doubts and search for answers.<br><br>And of course the <b>love story</b> is kind of sweet, with the ups and downs - I just wish they have realized sooner that they like each other and not make so many self-assumptions.<br><br>One more thing I want to add:<br>- Chloe seemed to have something in common with Bianca from "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931356.The_Duff_Designated_Ugly_Fat_Friend" title="The Duff Designated Ugly Fat Friend by Kody Keplinger" rel="nofollow noopener">The DUFF</a>";<br>- Lissa was as much as a 'control freak' as Natalie from "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7958702.Not_That_Kind_Of_Girl" title="Not That Kind Of Girl by Siobhan Vivian" rel="nofollow noopener">Not That Kind Of Girl</a>", a story that I found somehow similar to this one in many aspects.<br><br>All in one - a great read. I enjoyed this book from the first page to the last one and I am waiting for Kody's new book now :D <br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kody-keplinger/shut-out-review.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11602692883703340024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294942174?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294942174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14467501251805565593"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “You can't control everything. Sometimes you just need to relax and have faith that things will work out. Let go a little and just let life happen.” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/shut%20out%20collage.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433120979i/15052785.png' alt=' photo shut out collage.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Lissa has a problem. Her boyfriend Randy keeps putting her second to a stupid rivalry between the football players and the soccer players at her high school. Every time they make out in his car it gets egged, he leaves dates early for retaliation attacks and so on. Lissa isn't the only one fed up, all of the girlfriends for boys on</span>
  <span id="freeText14467501251805565593" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “You can't control everything. Sometimes you just need to relax and have faith that things will work out. Let go a little and just let life happen.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/shut%20out%20collage.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433120979i/15052785.png" alt=" photo shut out collage.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Lissa has a problem. Her boyfriend Randy keeps putting her second to a stupid rivalry between the football players and the soccer players at her high school. Every time they make out in his car it gets egged, he leaves dates early for retaliation attacks and so on. Lissa isn't the only one fed up, all of the girlfriends for boys on both of the teams are done. So Lissa comes up with a plan: no sex until the rivalry ends.<br><br>But with this no sex plan comes consequences and the girls learn which boys they can trust once sex is removed. On top of that Lissa now has to work with Cash, a boy from the soccer team and who she once had a crush on before she got with Randy.<br><br><b> <i> “You amaze me Lissa Daniels. Most girls would cave as soon as I gave them the puppy-dog look with these amazing eyes."<br>"Sorry. I like boys. Not dogs. You should've dated a different girl if you wanted someone to bend to your will.” </i> </b><br><br>A modern day Lysistrata, I expected to love this book and only ended up liking it. It lacked the emotional punch that usually comes with Keplinger's books, and Cash as a hero seemed so clueless most of the time that I wanted to punch him. As with all of Kody's books I was sucked in by the writing and finished this book in a matter of hours, but it wasn't a big winner for me. Maybe a little winner.<br><br>I will say as a person who works in libraries, and I worked my way from the bottom up I got a little nitpicky about Lissa's job as a shelver in a library while reading. I've never known any job title to be a shelver, it's a page who does that work. And pages almost never ever shelve together, they get their own sections and carts and it's a solitary job. So the scenes where Cash and Lissa keep getting put together shelving we not realistic for me. And before y'all attack me I know it's a book it's not real life, but it took me out of the story and that took away from the believability in the book for me.<br><br><b> <i> “Sometimes it's hard to predict who will make a person happy. But in the end, that's what matters.” </i> </b><br><br>I also wanted a bit more from the plot in terms of Lissa's family relationship, her dad and brother were strong side characters and I felt they were underutilized. And we only scratched the surface of Kelsey and Cash as other side characters. The focus kept being solely on Lissa and Randy and I kid of wish the author had written more.<br><br>This review is sounding like a bitch fest. I really did enjoy reading, and I don't regret reading it, but it's not something I would readily recommend to other readers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14467501251805565593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1242009825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242009825" />
    <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela"><img alt="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487543962p2/28640648.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1242009825?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa (Ever So Mela)" href="/user/show/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela">Melissa (Ever So Mela)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28640648-melissa-ever-so-mela?shelf=triangle-of-hell">triangle-of-hell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1242009825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9737530462366082904"> <b>3.5</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433197253i/15062836.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>How to write a fun YA contemporary? </b><br/><br/>Well, just follow Kody Keplinger's recipe cause she's got it down to a science!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433198139i/15062967.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I'm serious. They'll call me a pussy."<br/>"And if you help them, I'll call you a dick. So no matter what you do, you're going to be some form of genitalia.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>She was constantly cracking me up with her dry humor. And what I loved most about her? She felt like a real teenager who at times-let's be honest, more often than not- made mistakes.<br/>She was also strong. She wasn't pe</span>
  <span id="freeText9737530462366082904" style="display:none"> <b>3.5</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433197253i/15062836.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>How to write a fun YA contemporary? </b><br><br>Well, just follow Kody Keplinger's recipe cause she's got it down to a science!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433198139i/15062967.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I'm serious. They'll call me a pussy."<br>"And if you help them, I'll call you a dick. So no matter what you do, you're going to be some form of genitalia.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>She was constantly cracking me up with her dry humor. And what I loved most about her? She felt like a real teenager who at times-let's be honest, more often than not- made mistakes.<br>She was also strong. She wasn't perfect or had some constant God-sent advice for all her problems. She sounded real, and yes, I was annoyed with her at times, but when I sit back and think about how I was at that age, I have to admit, I was a pain in the ass too.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433198139i/15062968.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I didn’t do this to end the fighting. I did it because I know it’s important to you. And you’re important to me.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><u>This was what made me fall in love with the book</u>. Not the boyfriend, the high school drama or even the plot. It was the effin amazing friends that surround her! The friendships were breathtakingly beautiful and I don't mean in their perfection but in their realness. I mean I know that Chloe was one of the supporting characters but to be honest she could have been the lead for all I care. <u>That's how much I loved her</u>. Effin goldmine here. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I’ll always come if you want me to, Liss.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>And that's the thing, she didn't only have one amazing friend. If you've read other reviews you'll know I usually rant about the fact that nowadays authors tend to only make the female lead and her best friend the only characters you like. <b>But Kody Keplinger</b> managed to wow me with countless friends and thank the Lord with the absence of the cliche mean girl. She was able to give depth to not only Lissa(which btw her name's Melissa, just felt like I had to point it out :P) but to every character. They're all distinct in their own ways. Can I hear a hallelujah?!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433268117i/15074771.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"Because I want to see you with someone better than him. Someone who will see how lucky they are to have you."<br>I bit my lip, nervous but determined to ask my next question. "Do you happen to have someone particular in mind, Cash?"<br>"Maybe."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>I'm not even gonna gush but<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380358614ra/709788.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I don't know what the heck is wrong with me lately but I am <b>falling hard</b> for good guys and Cash is freaking amazeballs amazing! <b>
  <i>AMAZEBALLS AMAZING!</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433269272i/15074943.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Chloe didn't have all the answers, either. I knew that now. But she had known something all along that I hadn't: that being ashamed of what you want or how you feel is pointless, and letting anyone else make you feel ashamed is a waste. We all wanted different things, and that was okay. Chloe wanted sex without commitment. Mary wanted to wait until she was ready. And I wasn't sure what I wanted, but I didn't want to make any decisions until I knew. And I was proud of that.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>I don't know if you've ever noticed that most YA kind of fall flat. I mean, it's not like I expect great wonders from these books or anything but I do tend to expect some difference in the characters as the book progresses, especially if the point of the plot has some kind of maturity(not that this plot was mature or anything, sex strike is not a sensible way to go). What I mean is some plots tend to lead the characters to growing up and finding themselves. <b>This was one of them</b>. And we see her growth in the way she learns to deal with her family, in the way she starts to accept herself and in the way she starts to carry herself as a person. <u>And I loved that.</u><br><br><b>And finally...</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433269272i/15074944.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Do you know how sometimes books are preachy or you feel like the author is just shoving their own beliefs down your throat as you read the book? You know how sometimes it's annoying as heck? Well, while it may feel like the author is driving her advice home through these characters, <b>I couldn't help but wholeheartedly agree</b>.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“It's so screwed up, the standards...You should like it, but you shouldn't like it too much or talk about how much you like it. You should do it, but you shouldn't do it with too many people or talk about how much you're doing it. It's like there are so many rules, but none of them make sense.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>We're taught at a young age that sex is a taboo subject. That it shouldn't be broadcast like some news at 6. We're taught to judge a girl's worth by the amount of guys she's slept with but at the same time taught to admire guys because of how many women he's been able to take to bed. Girls are taught that if you like sex too much, you're a whore but if you don't like it you're a prude. Guys are taught that the more women you sleep with, the cooler you'll be and if you don't like to sleep around then obviously you must be gay. <br><b>Sometimes life and choices aren't as black and white.</b> And I loved how Shut Out portrayed it. <br><br><br>In the end it wasn't perfect but it did manage to make me think. And if that's something I could take away from a YA contemporary romance then <b>great</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9737530462366082904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1237765151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237765151" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237765151?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like battle of the sexes type books...or Duff</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover">don-t-be-fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=it-aint-easy-bein-cheesy">it-aint-easy-bein-cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237765151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9020865686791960920"><b>
  <i>"Because." Cash's fingers stilled, resting lightly against the back of my head, which didn't hurt anymore. He looked down at me for a long second before continuing. "Because I want to see you with someone better than him. Someone who will see how lucky they are to have you."<br/>I bit my lip, nervous but determined to ask my next question. "Do you happen to have someone particular in mind, Cash?"<br/>"Maybe."</i>
</b><br/><br/>4 days, three (attempted) books, and countless exaggerated sighs later, and I can't get this a</span>
  <span id="freeText9020865686791960920" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"Because." Cash's fingers stilled, resting lightly against the back of my head, which didn't hurt anymore. He looked down at me for a long second before continuing. "Because I want to see you with someone better than him. Someone who will see how lucky they are to have you."<br>I bit my lip, nervous but determined to ask my next question. "Do you happen to have someone particular in mind, Cash?"<br>"Maybe."</i>
</b><br><br>4 days, three (attempted) books, and countless exaggerated sighs later, and I can't get this author's characters out of my head. You heard me right-I have read two other books since finishing <b>DUFF</b> and nothing compares. I even tried to break back into my normal genre....but nothing seemed to stand up to the quirky inner dialogue of the heroines that this author creates. And, I'll be the first to admit it, her male leads are unforgettable. First, Wesley. And now, Cash Sterling??? Seriously?? I mean, no, they aren't amazing or crazy memorable, but they are sweet, endearing, kind-they fall hard for the female leads and they have the confidence and cockiness that gives them that sexy little edge that I have been missing, lately. My point to all this?? I read two other books, fully, before this, and I literally skipped their reviews (don't worry, I'll go back to them this week) to write this one. Because <b>when a book makes me feel good...that's all that matters</b>-and this book made me smile ear to ear.<br><br><b>"Lissa," Cash said slowly, drawing out the A at the end of my name. "Correct me if I'm wrong, but...Did you just mark a typo in your book?"<br>I bit my lip. "No. Of course not. Why would you say that?"<br>"Because you just marked something on the page with a red ink pen-like the ones teachers use to check papers."<br>"No, I didn't."<br>"Lissa."</b><br><br>5 stars. Sigh. It feels so wrong, but oh so right. I went to put a four, because, come on, how juvenile is this plot?? More than once I tried to imagine any one of my friends picking this up and not rolling their eyes...unsuccessfully, I might add. But then I thought to myself, WTF do I care what people think??? When I have a specific book type in my head, it's literally the only kind of book that will get a good rating from me. <b>Lately? My choice of poison has been high school drama, sexy boys who have the sweetest touch of possessiveness while not 100% being in a relationship with the main girl, and fun friendships that keep the main character afloat.</b> I dunno. It's perfect for my mood right now. <br><br><b>"It's not silly," he said. "What's silly is my deep-seated and unreasonable fear of fish."<br>I frowned. "Fish? Like food?"<br>"No, that doesn't bother me so much. Fish that are alive. I can't swim in lakes or rivers or anything besides a swimming pool because I'm always convinced the fish are swimming all over me...all slimy and...ugh."<br>I laughed, and Cash smiled.<br>"We all have our quirks," he said. "This is yours. You wouldn't be you without it."</b><br><br>I think the reason I'm so skeptical as to whether other people I know would love this story (I know most of my friends are like me and could overlook any idiosyncrasies and dumb shit in DUFF, because, well, <b>Wesley</b>) or not is the amount of cliches that overflow in these books. I mean, I'm the QUEEN of not liking cliches (Hmm well, no, maybe not, but I roll my eyes sometimes, I swear!!) but for some reason, this author makes the stupidest things, like, say, this war they have going on in the book, seem almost charming. And my biggest warning to anyone who trusts my thoughts or reviews??? This book is <b>dangerously cheesy.</b> It has alll the cheese!!! But only the <b>best</b> kind of cheese.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/pPfGmGV_zpsunkdxram.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427721584ra/14311785.gif" alt=" photo pPfGmGV_zpsunkdxram.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, here's the plot, in a nutshell. Lissa has a douchey boyfriend, Randy. Randy is on the football team. The football team and the soccer team have this epic (not so epic, it's more moronic-me and the girls agree on this front) rivalry that's been going on for years and years....and, while the biggest problem the girls see is that the boys put this childish rivalry ahead of 'together time', it's becoming more than that. People are kind of getting hurt-it's no longer just an emotional thing. And so, after being put second for the final time, Lissa decides enough is enough. She gathers all the girlfriends of the football and soccer players and induces a strike. What kind of strike, you ask?? Well, it's simple: <b>No more sex until the rivalry is over.</b> *insert eyeroll* Right?? It sounds soooo juvenile. And, in a way, it is. But then again, I didn't find it to be so-this author has a way of making it all seem...authentic. Authentic as any teenage melodrama could be. And, hold the eye rolling, I actually really enjoyed this plot. <b>It put the skeezers in the lime light and showed what boys were truly in love with their girls....and what boys just wanted an opportunity to be with certain, aforementioned girls</b>, like, say...Lissa?? <br><br><b>I could just make out the boys' retreating backs as they skirted across Ellen's backyard and out toward the gravel back roads of Hamilton. The moonlight framed their silhouettes, and for a moment, one paused. I could see him turning his head back, but he was too far off for me to recognize his face as he looked at the house. At the window. At me.<br>Somehow, I knew it was Cash.</b><br><br>Cash. Cash Sterling. What a sweetheart. He got under my skin, deep. I won't say he weaseled his way deeper than Wesley in my heart, but he got a nice little spot in the corner, saved all just for him. He was the guy always in the background, always secretly supporting Lissa and helping her when she fell. <b>He was the guy that when her heart got broken time and again, he silently helped her pick up the pieces.</b> I absolutely adored the way he treated her, the way he looked at her. I loved the way he was, just in general. I only wish we'd have gotten more time with him...though, the way it all happened seemed to be perfect, just as it was.<br><br><b>My body was riddled with electric shocks as his kisses grew more intense. My fingers grasped at his short brown hair, pulling him to me. I'd never felt like this, like I wanted to climb into another person's skin. Like I wanted every inch of him to touch every inch of me, to twine myself around him and never let go. I'd never kissed anyone this way.</b><br><br>So, yeah. I really enjoyed this. It had tons of stuff that was moronic, naturally, with that kind of plot...but I loved it, all the same. The biggest problem I see people having is the assumptions. Assuming it was all a game. Assuming 'he' thought he was too good for her. Assuming that kiss wasn't real. Not talking to each other about what they really felt for one another or what happened in the past...it's a killer. But, eh. I enjoyed this WAY too much to nitpick. It is what it is-I paid for cheap thrills and wanted petty high school drama. I got it. <i>*singing voice*</i> Drammmaaaaaaaa.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_inline_ml4ozi1Ihn1qz4rgp_zpszg0xvw7w.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1427736841ra/14315094.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_ml4ozi1Ihn1qz4rgp_zpszg0xvw7w.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>

<div id="review_3624482036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3624482036" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3624482036?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3624482036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer717723215443260078">I would love to see this book become a movie someday. It’s the kind of teenage romantic drama/comedy that is perfect for a period like this one we’re in. <br/><br/>It’s the battle of the sexes at Hamilton High. The football and soccer male players have a rivalry that is starting to really affect Lissa and her relationship with Randy. She comes up with a plan to end it and joins forces with the players’ girlfriends in order to execute it. The idea: withhold sexual activity until the rivalry is over.<br/><br/>It was </span>
  <span id="freeText717723215443260078" style="display:none">I would love to see this book become a movie someday. It’s the kind of teenage romantic drama/comedy that is perfect for a period like this one we’re in. <br /><br />It’s the battle of the sexes at Hamilton High. The football and soccer male players have a rivalry that is starting to really affect Lissa and her relationship with Randy. She comes up with a plan to end it and joins forces with the players’ girlfriends in order to execute it. The idea: withhold sexual activity until the rivalry is over.<br /><br />It was supposed to be clear and effective, but what Lissa did not see coming was that the boys would strike back with their own plan and that Cash—who she wishes she could forget about—would be part of it. Will this new battle end before someone’s relationship is destroyed or will this be the new normal at Hamilton High?<br /><br />I found this concept very original. There are a lot of high school dramas out there in the literature world, but this is the first time I read about something similar. Of course, the love-triangle is nothing new, but the discussion on sex and sexuality is. Kody Keplinger emphasises, through this story, the normality of having different sexual preferences. That it’s okay to have sex but also not to have it, to love it but also to dislike it. I quite enjoyed the overall openness of the author, and while I saw a lot coming regarding the plot, it was a fairly easy read that took my mind off of some stuff. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="717723215443260078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_619404857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619404857" />
    <a title="Monisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13001527-monisha"><img alt="Monisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433436407p2/13001527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619404857?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monisha" href="/user/show/13001527-monisha">Monisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=sweet-romances">sweet-romances</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=high-school-drama">high-school-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619404857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15449861118342688532">Shut Out is loosely based on the retelling of <b>Aristophanes’ Lysistrata</b>;<br/>Lissa is sick and tired of the rivalry between the soccer and football team, it’s been running almost like forever.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422167i/839582.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But now it’s seriously getting out of hand, it’s coming in between her relationship with Randy, her boyfriend.<br/><br/>So Lissa comes up with a plan to get all the soccer and football player’s girlfriends together and go on a "strike".<br/><br/><b>A SEX STRIKE!!!</b><br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422167i/839583.png' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/> <br/>It’s bound to get the boys so wound up that they will put an end to t</span>
  <span id="freeText15449861118342688532" style="display:none">Shut Out is loosely based on the retelling of <b>Aristophanes’ Lysistrata</b>;<br>Lissa is sick and tired of the rivalry between the soccer and football team, it’s been running almost like forever.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422167i/839582.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But now it’s seriously getting out of hand, it’s coming in between her relationship with Randy, her boyfriend.<br><br>So Lissa comes up with a plan to get all the soccer and football player’s girlfriends together and go on a "strike".<br><br><b>A SEX STRIKE!!!</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380422167i/839583.png" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <br>It’s bound to get the boys so wound up that they will put an end to their petty rivalry. <br><br>But then the boys put Cash (whose totally drop dead gorgeous may I add) as their leader and they start to fight back. But who will eventually cave and admit defeat?<br><br><i>And is Lissa getting far too involved than she should be? </i><br><br><br><b>
  <u>FIRST , THE GOOD:</u>
</b> <br><br><i>--&gt;Creative plot? Definitely. </i><br><br>Shut Out, was a good book, even though I thought <i>'woah high school girls?'</i>. It had a more 18+ just after high school feel for me. <br><br>I applaud Keplinger for writing so honestly and not shying away from the reality that <b>teens cuss and they have sex</b> ( And yes in a group, girls/women do talk candidly about sex).<br> <br><i>Probably more than most adults want to admit. </i><br><br>So, it is reality and it shouldn't be taboo to write about it. <br><br><br>I think that every girl can relate to one of the issues revolving around sex in this book, maybe more.<br><br><br>There is frank talk about teenage girls' sexual lives,<br>exploration of double standards,<br>it's okay to <b>not be ashamed</b> of who you are,<br>don't change yourself for a guy,<br>don't do something you're not comfortable with,<br>and you should always talk to someone if you're having a bad time, you'll feel better after - even if it's just your friends that you're talking to and an <i>inspiration from a classic</i> (I'm a sucker for modern re-tellings).<br><br><br><b>
  <u>Now, the bad:</u>
</b><br><br>1) It was just glaringly obvious she was at times extremely ego-centric. Said ego-centrism highlighted here:<br><br><i>“So, Homecoming,” I said loudly, interrupting a conversation Randy was having with Shane. I was sure it wasn’t important, anyway."</i><br><br>Yeah, I can see why two guys would want her...<br><br>2)During the strike, the girls talked about and treated the guys like they were <b>brain-dead puppies</b> who needed to be manipulated to serve a greater purpose and the guys, like in a lot of YA, were just "sex-sex-football-fight-sex" guys who of course have no feelings at all.<br><br>3)The story line was a bit predictable, but very cute anyhow.<br>It was <b>an one-dimensional YA book</b> to me.<br><br><br>But whatever. I still liked the book, not loved, but LIKED.<br><br>Shut Out was a good read.<br>It had it's frustrating moments, sigh worthy moments, and its hilarious moments; and the sex strike was ingenious.<br><br>So, a 3.5 stars from me.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15449861118342688532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_198722939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198722939" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198722939?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198722939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11829248693317732817">2 1/2 stars. <br/><br/>Original review posted on The Book Smugglers: <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2011/08/book-review-shut-out-by-kody-keplinge.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a><br/><br/>Shut Out is a modern-day retelling of Aristophanes’ Lysistrata, a classic Greek play about Lysistrata and her attempt to end the Peloponnesian War by persuading the women of the warring nations to withhold sex from their husbands in order to force peace negotiations. This foments a battle of the sexes as both sides try to stand their ground until eventually, the men give in and peace is achieved.<br/><br/>I was curious to see how Kody Keplinge</span>
  <span id="freeText11829248693317732817" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. <br /><br />Original review posted on The Book Smugglers: <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2011/08/book-review-shut-out-by-kody-keplinge.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a><br /><br />Shut Out is a modern-day retelling of Aristophanes’ Lysistrata, a classic Greek play about Lysistrata and her attempt to end the Peloponnesian War by persuading the women of the warring nations to withhold sex from their husbands in order to force peace negotiations. This foments a battle of the sexes as both sides try to stand their ground until eventually, the men give in and peace is achieved.<br /><br />I was curious to see how Kody Keplinger would deal with this premise in a modern context and especially with what I, personally, consider the most troubling aspects of the play when taken out of its historical context: 1) sex is more important to men than to women and women are able to withstand lack of sexual release more easily; and 2) the fact that sex can be used as a feminine weapon.<br /><br />In Shut Out the “war” is a ten-year-long rivalry between the football team and the soccer team at Hamilton High School. The heroine of the novel is Lissa and she is sick and tired of competing for her boyfriend’s attention. Randy is the quarterback of the school and even though he loves her, he doesn’t seem to love her enough to put her first. Lissa then concocts this plan and rallies all the girlfriends to join her on a hookup strike. As the battle rages on, the girls become friends and share their fears and hopes about sex and boys whilst Lissa becomes disillusioned with Randy and falls in love with another guy, Cash Sterling.<br /><br />I am troubled by this novel.<br /><br />On the one hand there are quite a few positive things about it. The novel is honestly quite fun if one can disregard the premise and the potentially problematic aspects that stem from it. The romance that develops between Cash Sterling (quite possibly the cheesiest character’s name in the history of cheesiness and therefore I am torn between finding it ridiculous or awesome. Maybe awesomely ridiculous?) and Lissa is quite sweet and I genuinely rooted for the two of them. I also breezed through the book quite easily.<br /><br />The most positive aspect of the novel however, was definitely the frank discussions about sex that the girls had once the feud starts and the friendship that grows between them. There is an exploration about slut shaming and how harmful and unfair it is especially when considering that boys grow a positive reputation for the same sort of experience that the girls are shamed for. There are conversations about the fact that there is no normal when it comes to sex: that being a virgin is ok, that not being a virgin is ok; that liking sex is awesome and not liking it or not being prepared for it is ok too. Even though some of it comes across as perhaps too message-heavy, the overall message about sex is a very positive message that I completely, 100% agree with.<br /><br />On the other hand and I am aware how is going to sound ridiculous considering that this is the very premise of the novel, it troubles me that in a modern context, sex is the weapon that girls chose to wield. That they couldn’t think of anything else they could do to stop the rivalry between the two teams like for example: youtube campaigns, riots and pickets, conversations or rallies, engaging other people in this conversation, bringing in TV crews, or radio crews to report on this ridiculous feud and so on and so forth.<br /><br />It is easy to accept that aspect of the original play considering the fact that the play was written over two thousand years ago in a time where women had little political power and could not affect the outcome of the war in any other possible way. It is much harder to accept that this is the only way they can think of to stop this war (which is not even a war AT ALL, only a silly rivalry) in a modern context. Not a single girl even offers an alternative.<br /><br />Although it is brought up at different points that it is wrong to use sex as a weapon, I felt this was only partly addressed when some of the girls used it to seduce and leave the boys hanging on. I feel that there is much more to sexual politics and sex being used as a feminine weapon than simply giving guys blue balls.<br /><br />Further to that, despite all the positive messages about sex and girls, and how things are complex and there is a myriad of ways of dealing with it all, I think that the main assumption that the girls can withhold sex more easily than boys goes largely unchecked. There is the idea that boys would do anything for sex, that girls are more in control and unfortunately it reeks of gender essentialism and I am unconvinced that this was explored or truly addressed in depth. This is even more plain when you consider that not a single one of these girls seem to play any sports, that the girls swear their oath on an issue of Cosmos and the boys on an issue of Sports Illustrated and that the girls seem to be more frustrated when the boys withhold conversation from them.<br /><br />In the end, despite the obvious positive aspects, I felt dissatisfied with the novel as a whole. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11829248693317732817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_202173061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/202173061" />
    <a title="Lanica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1336787-lanica"><img alt="Lanica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1217471726p2/1336787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1336787-lanica?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer202173061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13292840513115906790">PERSONAL REVIEW: Wow! Is that really what High School is like these days? I'm getting old!<br/><br/>SCHOOL LIBRARIAN REVIEW: I think parents who opened this up to some random page and started reading might have some issues with this book. If I put this on my library shelves, I'd expect someone - at some point - to complain...or even challenge this book. And, I might have to agree, which is why this book would not be one I would purchase for my school library.<br/><br/>First off let me say that this has an overall g</span>
  <span id="freeText13292840513115906790" style="display:none">PERSONAL REVIEW: Wow! Is that really what High School is like these days? I'm getting old!<br /><br />SCHOOL LIBRARIAN REVIEW: I think parents who opened this up to some random page and started reading might have some issues with this book. If I put this on my library shelves, I'd expect someone - at some point - to complain...or even challenge this book. And, I might have to agree, which is why this book would not be one I would purchase for my school library.<br /><br />First off let me say that this has an overall good message. Be yourself. Don't let other people make you do things you are not willing to do. Be an individual. Think for yourself. Think! But, that being said, this book is not for everyone.<br /><br />The girlfriends of both the soccer and football teams all agree to withhold sex until the rivalry between the teams is quashed. <br /><br />I have a few problems with the premise:<br />*It assumes that the girls are all having sex, only one comes out as being a virgin and she is treated poorly when she says so.<br />*It assumes that the girls are not a part of the rivalry. I know that in many cases girls are a lot more mean-spirited than boys and it's unlikely that they are all going to want the same ends here.<br />*It assumes that none of the girls are in sports of their own. They are all available after school for the games and shopping or whatever, but not one girl is said to be involved in extracurriculars of their own of any kind.<br /><br />The idea that the girls are afraid to talk about sex, but the 'sex strike' makes them open up to one another is a good idea, but it doesn't really help the girls who are likely to read the book understand anything that they may need in real life. The girls say, "I don't like it" or "I'm afraid" or whatever, and a girl who reads this book will say, yeah...me, too. But then the writer does nothing to help the reader truly understand the issues. It had the potential to be life-changing...instead, it's just fluff.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13292840513115906790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer8074322448167084088">What seemed like a silly premise turned out to be something relevant but still very entertaining at the same time. I was kind of impressed really. The main plot, girls agreeing on a sex-strike against boys to end the rivalry between football and soccer players is pretty funny especially when the boys were trying to fight back, seducing the girls by taking off their shirts. Lol. But as the story pushes through, it becomes not only about just the “war”. <br/><br/>I didn’t think so much into <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10757771.Shut_Out' title='Shut Out by Kody Keplinger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shut Out</a> but as </span>
  <span id="freeText8074322448167084088" style="display:none">What seemed like a silly premise turned out to be something relevant but still very entertaining at the same time. I was kind of impressed really. The main plot, girls agreeing on a sex-strike against boys to end the rivalry between football and soccer players is pretty funny especially when the boys were trying to fight back, seducing the girls by taking off their shirts. Lol. But as the story pushes through, it becomes not only about just the “war”. <br /><br />I didn’t think so much into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10757771.Shut_Out" title="Shut Out by Kody Keplinger" rel="nofollow noopener">Shut Out</a> but as I keep turning the pages, the story becomes more meaningful. I admire the light and yet impactful take on feminism and gender equality. Girls looking out for other girls. The friendship bit is quite admirable really. <br /><br />I like the narrative’s straightforwardness and honesty and I really appreciate that it’s about doing away with labels and stereotypes. Not a lot of YA books openly talk about sex but this book managed to do that without making it embarrassing. I actually think it’s quite informative and helpful especially to young adults on the verge of wanting to know more about their sexuality and don’t know whom to talk to about these things.<br /><br />There is also an underlying theme on grief that resulted to <b>Lissa</b>’s (the main character) control issues which kind of where all the events including the conflicts in the story rooted from and I’m glad that by end of the story, she learns to let herself loose a bit, embrace life and risks including involving herself with the really cute and adorable <b>Cash</b>. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3629869821211214629">First, the good: frank talk about teenage girls' sexual lives, exploration of double standards, inspiration from a classic (I'm a sucker for modern re-tellings).<br/><br/>The bad? It took me a long while to feel as if I could relate to the protagonist at all. It seemed like her only personality trait for a good portion of the book was having a boyfriend. Finally, we find out she's also a control freak who works in a library (just like me! ha!) <br/><br/>But seriously, the fact that every single girl in this book (w</span>
  <span id="freeText3629869821211214629" style="display:none">First, the good: frank talk about teenage girls' sexual lives, exploration of double standards, inspiration from a classic (I'm a sucker for modern re-tellings).<br /><br />The bad? It took me a long while to feel as if I could relate to the protagonist at all. It seemed like her only personality trait for a good portion of the book was having a boyfriend. Finally, we find out she's also a control freak who works in a library (just like me! ha!) <br /><br />But seriously, the fact that every single girl in this book (with the exception of the "slut") has an athlete boyfriend really bugged me. They talk about the question of what is normal for a teenage girl in terms of sex. There's the girl who does it with her boyfriend, the girl who does "everything but" with her boyfriend, the girl who is waiting to do it with her boyfriend, and the girl who does it with lots of guys but doesn't tie herself down to one boyfriend. What about the plain ol' girl who has no guy (or guys) in her sex life? If I'd read this when I was a teenager, I'd tell all these chicks to shut up and stop complaining. At least you have boyfriends! The grownup me realizes that half of their boyfriends are total dicks.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12188126379670825964">I'm still trying to figure out how to review this. I read and finished it a few days ago and I thought it was good and I mean really good. I was really hesitant to pick this up because I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931356.The_DUFF_Designated_Ugly_Fat_Friend_' title='The DUFF (Designated Ugly Fat Friend) by Kody Keplinger' rel='nofollow noopener'>The DUFF</a> and really didn't like it, I didn't like the writing, the characters or the plot, I basically didn't like the book. SO you can see why I was pretty hesitant to pick up Shut Out. But boy am I glad that I did.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Shut out is about Lissa, a girl who is constantly reminded of the ongoing feud between the s</span>
  <span id="freeText12188126379670825964" style="display:none">I'm still trying to figure out how to review this. I read and finished it a few days ago and I thought it was good and I mean really good. I was really hesitant to pick this up because I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931356.The_DUFF_Designated_Ugly_Fat_Friend_" title="The DUFF (Designated Ugly Fat Friend) by Kody Keplinger" rel="nofollow noopener">The DUFF</a> and really didn't like it, I didn't like the writing, the characters or the plot, I basically didn't like the book. SO you can see why I was pretty hesitant to pick up Shut Out. But boy am I glad that I did.<br /><br /><br /><br />Shut out is about Lissa, a girl who is constantly reminded of the ongoing feud between the soccer and football teams in her school [spoilers removed], her and the other girls dating the guys on the teams decide that they have had enough. They go on a strike, a sex strike to be exact. They are with holding sex until the bouts stop the feud. It soon turns into an all out war. [spoilers removed]<br /><br /><br /><br />I liked the plot, it was kind of a modern telling of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1591.Lysistrata" title="Lysistrata by Aristophanes" rel="nofollow noopener">Lysistrata</a>, the greek play where women withheld sex from their husbands until they stopped going to war. The women won in the end (I read the play). I liked the writing more than I liked the writing in The Duff and the characters had their flaws, boy did they have a lot of flaws. But in a way, those flaws made me like the characters more. It made them real.<br /><br /><br /><br />Overall, it was a good read and I read it all in one sitting. I recommend it to YA lovers, romance lovers and people looking for a funny/ fluffy/ interesting/ nice/ readable/ enjoyable book. Because if that's what your looking for, look no further. This is it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12188126379670825964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207028235" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7692556174204458541">I was afraid to read <i>Shut Out</i> because friend of mine was disappointed after reading it. But I'm happy that I read it - it was refreshing novel in the flood of young adult fiction. I recommend this book to all teen girls, and to some girls over twenties, who have some issues with sex and what is expected of them when it comes to it. Ending is the only thing that I was... how to put it...sarcastic, maybe? I know you writers want to make us satisfied, so, obviously, you give us happy endings. But i</span>
  <span id="freeText7692556174204458541" style="display:none">I was afraid to read <i>Shut Out</i> because friend of mine was disappointed after reading it. But I'm happy that I read it - it was refreshing novel in the flood of young adult fiction. I recommend this book to all teen girls, and to some girls over twenties, who have some issues with sex and what is expected of them when it comes to it. Ending is the only thing that I was... how to put it...sarcastic, maybe? I know you writers want to make us satisfied, so, obviously, you give us happy endings. But in the real life, things don't end that way. Girl who sleeps with more boys than it's by some twisted social standards acceptable is still a slut, and guy doing the same thing is <i>the man</i>. But most unnerving thing is this - girls are the biggest enemies to each other - they are first to call someone slut or whore or easy. They hide the truth about their sex lives, they are feeding all those double standards instead to fight them. <br />So, my dear girls all around the world, stop acting like fucking prudes! We all love sex! We are all doing it! Next time, don't stand on sidelines and let someone judge a girl you know because she sleeps with her boyfried (it's normal! What? Like you are just going to stare into each other eyes for a whole year? Get serious, please!) </span>
